Balloon Advertising Not Allowed by the Public Works Department

In recent times, commercial competition relies on promotion, and advertising methods are changing with each passing day. Recently, a foreigner named Sparks proposed to the Public Works Department of the Public Concession to launch a balloon advertising business in Shanghai and requested the approval of the Public Works Department. This matter was discussed by the Garrison Committee some time ago. It was generally believed that this novel advertisement was dangerous and had many drawbacks. It was feared that the balloon would leak gas and catch fire in the downtown area, or even explode, thereby endangering buildings and property on the ground, and that it would easily come into contact with electrical wires, causing all kinds of accidents. Moreover, when the balloon is stationed in the sky, passers-by and drivers would often stop to look up, their minds scattered, which could easily cause accidents. It was also felt that it would be difficult to approve. Moreover, a similar proposal was made to the committee in mid-November last year, but it was not approved. Now that the old case has been brought up again, the nature is similar, and there is really no room for discussion. Therefore, this novel advertising technique was not approved by the Public Works Department and will not be seen by the people of Shanghai.

Qingyanggang Railway Hotel Launches Climbing Trip to Kunshan Maanshan

The Qingyanggang Railway Garden Hotel of the Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration will take advantage of the Sunday holiday to launch a climbing trip to Kunshan Maanshan this month on the 6th. If people from all walks of life in this city want to visit that place, they can take the 20th express train to Qingyang from Shanghai North Station at 9:00 am on that day. After getting off the train, enjoy the scenery on the harbor bank, and have lunch at the Railway Garden Hotel at 1:00 pm. At 1:00 pm in the afternoon, take a motorboat directly to the foot of Kunshan Maanshan, and climb up to overlook the scenery. At 4:30 pm, return to Qingyanggang and take the 11th express train back to Shanghai at 5:22 pm. If travelers want to go to Kunshan to climb the mountain first, they can take the 22nd express train from Shanghai North Station at 9:00 am on that day, get off at Kunshan Station, hire a rickshaw to Maanshan, and climb the mountain for sightseeing. Have lunch at a Kunshan restaurant, and at the same time, call the Qingyanggang Railway Garden Hotel (telephone Kunshan 180) to send a motorboat to wait at the foot of the mountain to take you to the Qingyanggang Railway Garden Hotel (you can enjoy the harbor scenery in the motorboat) to tour the scenery in the garden or have a meal. At 5:21 pm in the afternoon, take the 11th express train back to Shanghai.

Cai, Director of Public Security Bureau, Issues Order to Strictly Arrest Robbers in Post Office Robbery Case

Cai Jingjun, Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, has recently issued a special order to the sub-bureaus and teams under his jurisdiction regarding the major robbery case at the Postal Administration (Order No. Zhengzi 3505): "According to a public letter from the Shanghai Municipal Party Executive Committee based on a petition from the Postal Workers' Union, it was found that the Shanghai Postal Administration was robbed by several bandits at around 10:00 am on the 9th of this month. More than 91,000 yuan, which the post office was about to load into a car and transport to the Savings and Remittance Bureau on Fuzhou Road, was swept away. One clerk was shot and killed, and two guards were killed and one wounded. Such a major robbery has shocked the union members. The post office is an important place for office work, so ten patrolmen from the Public Security Bureau are stationed there daily for security. However, the stationed patrolmen are incompetent, slack in prevention, allowing the bandits to mix in. Moreover, when the guards were fighting with the bandits, the stationed patrolmen all hid and refused to resist, which is even more dereliction of duty. Now that this case has been going on for more than ten days, the perpetrators are still at large and have not been arrested, which will cause the citizens to have doubts about the city's security in the future. The union members serve the postal service and are very concerned about this case. They are dissatisfied with the police authorities' lack of prevention, lack of courage to resist, and inability to arrest the perpetrators. The first executive meeting of the union has resolved to petition the head office to transfer to the Public Security Bureau to solve the case within a time limit to uphold the law and order and restore security, etc. Based on this, the case involves robbery and homicide, and it is appropriate to send a letter to your bureau to instruct your subordinates to strictly arrest the perpetrators and bring them to justice."

Increased Telephone Fees

Chinese and Japanese Users Voice Opposition in Unison. Expert General Report Largely Completed.

Central News Agency reports: The issue of the Shanghai Telephone Company's request to increase telephone fees has been studied by the Telephone Expert Committee, and the general report is now being compiled. Yesterday, the Public Works Department held a board meeting. Because the report has not yet been completed, the issue was not discussed. However, it is understood that the general report will be completed within a few days and submitted to the board of directors. The board of directors will then forward it to the Public Utility Committee for discussion. After a result is planned, it will be submitted to the board of directors for approval. Therefore, the submission of the Telephone Expert Committee's general report will still take some time. The majority of the general report has been drafted and completed. Although the per-call billing layer has not been completely decided, the attitudes of the British and American experts are converging, so the principle of per-call billing will definitely be adopted. Due to the depression of all industries and the increasingly sluggish market conditions, the city's users have long firmly opposed it. The Japanese residents of this city have also expressed their opposition to the per-call billing issue due to the decline in social economy.

The Continental Daily reports: According to British telephone expert Mr. Blanc, the Telephone Expert Committee's report will be submitted to the Public Works Department within two weeks. The committee invited formal groups of telephone users to submit suggestions, but none did so. Only a few individuals went to the committee's office briefly.

Truth of the Bizarre Homicide Remains Unclear

Luo Yusheng's Statements Half True and Half False, Investigation Difficult. Luo Himself Owns a Safe Deposit Box at the Shanghai Bank. The Red Spots on the Suit Pants, Analyzed, are Not Bloodstains. Police Request the Court to Extend the Investigation.

Luo Yusheng, a native of Yiwu, Zhejiang, who formerly worked as a lawyer, was assassinated and killed on June 10 last year in the Binhefang lane on Guangdong Road. His son, Luo Yusheng, is eleven years old and works as a teaching assistant at the Mingchen Elementary School at No. 21 Xinqiao Road in Nanshi. He is heavily suspected in the case of the murder of Jin Dai, a woman from Jinhua, and her daughter, Luo Guo, at No. 45 in the intersection of North Henan Road and Aierjin Road at 8:30 am on September 23 of this year. The investigation has been conducted by Hua Detective Shang Wu, Detective Zhao Qingkui, etc. from the Huishi Police. Luo Yusheng has been escorted to the Special Court and interrogated. The details have already been recorded in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, the case was further interrogated by Judge Liu Yugui in Criminal Court No. 8. The victim's family hired attorney Cheng Shangfeng to appear in court and file a civil lawsuit. The defendant Luo Yusheng hired attorneys Xu Jie and San to appear in court for defense. The police, during the postponement of this case, also obtained a formal letter from the court and transferred a suitcase and a radio from the Municipal Public Security Bureau. The box was deposited by the defendant Luo Yusheng at the home of Wang Mingrong at No. 14 Jiu'anli, Huangjiayu Road in Nanshi, and then transferred to the Public Security Bureau by Wang. The box contained valuables, including a silver handbag, two keys with the number 4261, a small diamond, a pair of jade-encrusted pearl earrings (50 pearls in total), a small pearl flower, a pair of pearl earrings, a bracelet, a necklace, a gold book ring, one hundred loose pearls, one red and one blue gem, a pearl ring, two jade rings, a 500-yuan deposit slip from the Zhejiang Xingye Bank, a 10,000-yuan passbook from Hengda Xiang, a 4,000-yuan passbook from Taihe Company, a passbook from the Tongyuan Bank (all under the name of Jin Xiaoji), a 2,400-yuan deposit ticket from the Shanghai Bank under the name of Luo Huangji, a savings account in the name of Luo Shenji at the Zhejiang Local Industrial Bank, and three seals of Jin Ling, Jin Zhao, and Jin Lingxian, etc., all of which were valuable. The police attorney Zhang Tianyin stated that during the postponement of the case, the police had thoroughly investigated various pieces of evidence. However, because the defendant's statements to the police were half true and half false, the investigation was quite difficult. The defendant had previously stated to the police that the suitcase and radio had been sent to Wang Mingrong's house, but he denied this during the court hearing. In addition to Wang Mingrong, who has already testified in court, there are also witnesses Cai Xingbao and Municipal Public Security Bureau patrol officer No. 8781 who can testify. When the incident occurred, the police detectives went to investigate. Jin Lingyi, the mother of the deceased Jin Dai (Baozhen), stated that two seals hidden in a teapot, a photo of Jin Lingyi herself, and a photo of Jin Youmai Bao Xing were stolen. Now, these items were found in the suitcase presented by Wang Mingrong. It was also found that the defendant had a safe deposit box at the Shanghai Bank with the number 1741, opened on September 2 of this year in the name of Jin Xinji. The police requested and were granted permission by the court to issue an official letter to the Shanghai Bank, and in the presence of a clerk, the box was opened. The box contained the defendant's father's seal and gold jewelry passbook, etc. Another safe deposit box belonging to the victim was stored, in the name of Dai Baozhen, with the number 426, which was also opened. It contained stock certificates of the Home Industry Cooperative and the Zhonghua Huashu Co., Ltd., etc. However, it was found that the box had been opened on the 1st of the previous month, which is consistent with the defendant's previous statement that the safe deposit box keys had been stolen ten days before the incident. There was also a trolley ticket found at the scene of the incident. The police investigated with the trolley company, and the result was that it was not a ticket from the 22nd, nor was it the defendant's. There was also a pair of suit pants found at the defendant's residence, with many red spots on the trouser legs. The police suspected that they were the deceased's bloodstains, so they were sent to the Public Works Department Health Office for analysis. The results of the analysis showed that there was no blood reaction, and it was not bloodstains. However, it could not be determined what the stains were. If the court believes that further analysis is necessary, the police will send it to an expert for analysis. The defendant previously stated to the police that the fugitive Xu Wenxian and a person surnamed Ma had committed the crime, but according to the police's speculation, Xu and Ma may not exist. The defendant must have colluded with another person to commit the crime himself. The deceased Jin Dai suffered a total of six knife wounds to the head, one knife wound to the right eye and neck, and three fingers on her right hand were cut off. The maid Luo Guo also suffered four knife wounds to the head and face. According to this situation, the perpetrators' methods were extremely fierce, and it seemed that they had planned to retaliate in advance. The defendant's statements that his father was killed and that the property was withheld by the Jin family, and that the defendant had repeatedly requested its return, etc., were consistent with the circumstances. After the postponement, on October 29, the defendant personally wrote a statement in the police station, admitting that he had gone with Xu Wenxian and a person surnamed Ma to kill Jin and others. Therefore, it is proposed that the court postpone the case again so that the police can conduct a detailed investigation during the postponement, in the hope of obtaining sufficient evidence. Therefore, Municipal Public Security Bureau police officer No. 8781 Yang Daocen testified that on September 23, I was stationed at the entrance of Jiu'anli, Huangjiaque Road. Between 12:00 noon and 2:00 pm, I saw the defendant riding a bicycle to No. 14 Yuan'anli, but I cannot remember whether he had any objects in his hand. Judge Liu questioned the defendant about this, and Luo replied that he was riding to play. Witness Wang Mingrong testified that I am the landlord of No. 14 Jiu'anli. The defendant came to rent the parlor room in May at a monthly rent of 12 yuan. He moved out on September 8. On September 23, at 10:30 am, the defendant came to rent the parlor room again, paid a rent of 10 yuan, and deposited a suitcase in the room. At 2:00 or 3:00 pm, the defendant also brought a radio. The next day, I saw news reports about Luo Yusheng's arrest and thought it was of great importance, so I reported it to the Public Security Bureau. When the defendant Luo Chusheng heard this, he admitted that he had gone to rent the house and deposit the radio, but denied that the suitcase was his. Judge Liu questioned him about the confession made at the police station and asked if it was written by him. The defendant replied that although it was written by him, it was under duress and not voluntary. He completely overturned his admission that he had colluded with others to kill Jin Dai, and only stated that although he suspected that Jin Dai was related to his father's murder last year, he had no substantial evidence, etc. Finally, witness Cai Xingfei testified that before the incident, the defendant had gone to the deceased's home to move a suitcase and radio, and that Cai had helped with the moving. Judge Liu verified the confessions. Since it was past noon and further analysis of the suit pants found at the defendant's residence was necessary, he ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody. The case was postponed for further hearing on the afternoon of October 9. The victim's lawyer stood up and stated that because the deceased's family could not afford the funeral expenses, he requested permission to have the Tongyuan Bank passbook released to Jin Lingyi for safekeeping. The court approved this. The court adjourned the session with the sounding of the clock.

Taxpayers' Association Sends Letter to Public Works Department Requesting Correction of Unfair Penalties

Due to the Health Office's One-Sided Acceptance of Garbage Headman's Report

The Public Concession Taxpayers' Chinese Association sent a letter to the Public Works Department yesterday: "Dear Sirs, According to a letter from Dai Guo'an of Yifeng Tobacco Shop, No. 4, Lane 1451, Xinzha Road, Yifeng Tobacco Shop has been established in the Concession for many years. Due to rent issues, it moved to Garage No. 4, Tongdeli, Lane 1451, Xinzha Road at the end of April of this year. The family lives separately at No. 16. Since the resumption of business, the search for rent has still been difficult, like a ram butting a fence, advancing and retreating being difficult. Unexpectedly, around the Dragon Boat Festival, a person speaking with a Jiangbei accent came to demand petty rules. The merchant was short on money and did not agree to his request. He left resentfully. After investigation, it was discovered that he was the garbage headman Gu Xiaoma of No. 33. His father is also engaged in this industry in the East District. The merchant did not suspect anything else. Unexpectedly, out of resentment, on August 20, Gu took advantage of his position to commit fraud, secretly inquired about the neighbor's servants, and openly copied the merchant's store number and house number, falsely reporting to the Public Works Department Health Office, falsely accusing the merchant's store of being unclean and violating regulations. Suddenly, on September 27, the merchant received a court summons. After reading it, the merchant was deeply surprised. Countless car-hiring shops are set up next to the Public Works Department's elementary school, and countless cars stop in front of the door. Students and maids enter and exit four times a day. In addition, there are various vendors, as dense as scales. The food and fruit peels are discarded all over the ground, and the broken paper scraps of the food purchased by the students returning home from the candy sales department set up in the school are also thrown on the store's must-pass road. The merchant pays extreme attention to cleanliness and sweeps all day long, never taking a break, as everyone knows and can be investigated. Furthermore, the wind blows leaves, which fall randomly. The garbage headman Gu Xiaoma, in order to fail to extort petty rules, harmed the merchant by relying on his power to make false accusations, and has no way to appeal. The authorities do not investigate and listen to one side of the story, suing in court for punishment, which is unbearable and unthinkable for people to live. Therefore, I sincerely ask your association to sympathize with the difficulties of the merchants, transfer a letter to the Public Works Department to correct it, and provide relief to the merchants, which is both a public virtue and convenient, etc. Having arrived at the association, the Health Office should investigate the accusations in detail and carefully examine the environment in which the accused is located. If it is indeed the act of the accused, then the punishment is justified, and the wind of false accusations out of resentment will naturally disappear. According to the letter, it is appropriate to send a letter to your department to quickly correct the Health Office's indiscriminate accusations and penalties."

Chinese Animal Protection Association to Hold a Solicitation and Promotion Convention Today

To be held at the City Chamber of Commerce at 2 PM. The Entire Country to Comply with the Executive Yuan's Order to Suspend Slaughter for One Day.

Today (the 4th) is World Animal Day. The Shanghai Chinese Animal Protection Association will hold its second Animal Protection Promotion Convention at the City Chamber of Commerce near Tianhou Palace Bridge at 1 PM this afternoon. At the same time, a membership solicitation convention will be held. In addition to inviting celebrities to give speeches and perform entertainment, special supplements will be published in major newspapers, lantern slides will be added to various movie theaters, and radio stations will broadcast promotional messages. The entire country will comply with the order to suspend slaughter for one day. The details are as follows:

Convention Ceremony

(1) Opening with music; (2) All stand at attention; (3) Sing the Party song; (4) Pay the highest respects to the Party, National Flag, and the portrait of the late Premier; (5) Reverently read the late Premier's will; (6) Silent tribute; (7) Opening address by the chairman; (8) Report; (9) Designation by Party and government organs; (10) Speeches (by Ye Gongchuo, Kong Xiangxi, Cai Jingjun, Dharma Master Taixu, and representatives from Western animal protection associations, etc.); (11) Closing remarks by the chairman; (12) Entertainment performances; (14) Dismissal with music.

Convention Staff

Presidium: Ye Gongchuo, Guan Jiongzhi, Wang Yishi, Kong Zhizhi, Huang Hanzhi, Xu Shiying, Wang Xiaolai, Zhong Ketuo, Zhang Yisheng; Master of Ceremonies: Pan Renwei; Recorders: Yao Huian, Zhang Yongbin; General Affairs Director: Li Jingwei; (Chief) Pan Renwei; (Deputy) Investigators: Zhou Minggeng, Du Zhuang , Zheng Mingrong, You Yingfu; Recruiters: Shen Binhan; (Director) Wu Meiping, Chen Mengfei, Chen Weiyao, Li Rensen, Chen Lixian, Shi Binsheng, Zhu , Zhu Shiseng, Zhang Youhua; Entertainment: Wu Zhimei, Hu Jiankun, Yan Zhuju, Hu Yongxin, Cao Yigong; Documentation: Yang Shuchu, He Rongbin; Logistics: Hou Haiming, Feng Liang , Zhang Jinan.

Significance of Promotion

In order to widely promote the significance of Animal Day, the association has specially arranged for Shen Bao, Xinwen Bao, and Min Bao, three major newspapers in Shanghai, to publish special supplements today. Local movie theaters in Shanghai will add promotional lantern slides. Slogans will be posted on trams. At the same time, all radio stations in the city will be specially engaged to broadcast lectures on Animal Day as a public service. The text of the lecture is as follows: Today is October 4th, which is also the annual World Animal Day. Animals have the same right to survive as we humans. However, humans often rely on their superior intelligence and strength to slaughter and kill weak animals for food, creating a cruel stain on human peace and rationality. Therefore, many sages and wise men in our country advocated the idea of ​​benevolence and love for all things thousands of years ago to teach people to be good. Mencius also said, "When I see its life, I cannot bear to see its death." This sentence clearly teaches people not to kill and not to abuse all animals. Various European and American countries have had organizations to protect animals for hundreds of years, vigorously advocating animal protection, and the government has enacted special laws. However, our country did not have such an organization until last year when the Chinese Animal Protection Association was established to promote animal protection. Today, the association is holding its second Animal Protection Promotion Convention at the City Chamber of Commerce. It is hoped that the audience will keep in mind the concept of ​​the unity of all things and love animals at all times and in all places, and that they will never arbitrarily abuse or kill them. This is the only way to show the benevolent spirit of humanity and restore the new life of our country's inherent virtues. From today onwards, I urge you all not to forget the meaning of this Animal Day.

Entertainment Program

(1) Music performance by the orphanage military band; (2) Speech by Liu Chunshan; (3) National music by the Postal Workers' Union; (4) Cantonese opera by Ms. Huang Cuiyu, Zhou Jieming, Yang Guisheng; (5) Comedy by the alumni of Renhui Primary School; (6) National music by the Zhonghua Jiande Association; (7) Harmonica by the alumni of Renhui Primary School; (8) Qin opera by Pan Renwei; (9) Music by the Mingyue Opera Troupe; (10) Animal protection song; (11) Love for life song; (12) Opera by the Mingyue Opera Troupe; (13) Singing by Ms. Bai Hong, Li Mingjian; (14) Magic by Xu Shengxiang.

One Day of Slaughter Suspension

Previously, the chairman of the association, Ye Gongchuo, submitted a request to the Executive Yuan's Ministry of Interior to issue an order to all provinces, cities, and counties across the country to suspend slaughter for one day on October 4th (today). In Shanghai, the Chinese area has been instructed by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and Public Security Bureau to comply. In the Special District, the Public Works Department has also agreed to issue a written notice to persuade slaughterhouses to comply, in order to show animal protection and provide a visual lesson. The original letter from the Public Works Department's representative, He Deqiu, replying to the Animal Protection Association, is recorded as follows: In response to your letter, we have received your letter stating that October 4th is World Animal Day, and your association is proposing to promote the animal protection movement. We would like to request the Public Works Department to issue an order on this day to prohibit the slaughter of all kinds of animals within its jurisdiction, in order to show animal protection and provide a visual lesson. We are extremely willing to support this. However, the Acting Director-General of our Bureau believes that, bound by established regulations, the Public Works Department has no authority to prohibit slaughter. This is the difference between the Chinese area and the concession. However, after consulting with the Director of the Health Department, he has agreed to issue a written notice to the slaughterhouses in the concession to persuade them to refrain from slaughtering for one day, in order to show animal protection and provide a visual lesson. We are writing this special letter to reply, hoping that you will take note of it. Sincerely, He Deqiu. October 2nd.

Yangjiadu Warehouse of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Suffers Huge Shortage of Goods

Over 500 Pieces of Miscellaneous Grain Missing. Warehouse Manager Dismissed and Shortages Investigated. New Warehouse Manager Lin Zhongzhen Takes Over.

The Yangjiadu warehouse of the state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company recently suffered a large-scale theft of goods. After the company discovered this, the warehouse manager was dismissed and investigated, and a new warehouse manager was appointed to take over. The details are as follows:

Changing Stacking of Intermodal Transport Goods

The state-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Longhai Railway intermodal transport goods were initially unloaded at the Jinliyuan Wharf warehouse. Later, because the warehouses on the southern wharves were filled with goods arriving from regular liner services from the North and South Seas and imported goods from Yangtze River steamers, they were insufficient. Therefore, the intermodal transport goods loaded from Lianyungang were changed to be stacked in the Yangjiadu Wharf warehouse. Ships from Laoyao were also unloaded at this warehouse, so most of the goods stacked there were goods transported from the Northwest.

Goods Missing from the Warehouse

Among the goods stored in the warehouse, miscellaneous grains transported from the Longhai Railway accounted for the majority. Recently, it was discovered that the warehouse had a shortage of more than 500 pieces of miscellaneous grains and other goods. It is not yet clear whether these missing goods were stolen. The company heard about this and first investigated the warehouse affairs department, confirming the facts. A report was made to General Manager Liu Hongsheng, who decided to conduct a thorough investigation of the shortage of goods.

Dismissing Warehouse Manager Jin

Warehouse Manager Jin Zeru should bear full responsibility for this matter, and the tally clerks also have considerable responsibility. Therefore, Warehouse Manager Jin Zeru was dismissed and investigated. At the same time, all goods stored in the warehouse were cleared, and a thorough investigation was conducted into the missing goods. According to the warehouse manager's statement to the company, when customers came to the warehouse to pick up goods, there were some shortages when the bags were changed, and the amount was huge, resulting in accumulated shortages. It was not the result of internal staff fraud.

New Warehouse Manager Takes Office

The company has appointed Lin Zhongzhen as the new warehouse manager of Yangjiadu. Lin has taken office. The deputy warehouse manager is a Mr. Li. The chief of the general affairs department of the company, together with the main staff members of the intermodal transport section of the warehouse affairs department, went to the Yangjiadu warehouse yesterday to review the stored goods. At the same time, they decided to conduct a thorough investigation into the missing goods to find out the truth.

Epiphyllum Opens in Zhongxi Girls' School Garden

Thirty-Five Blooms Opened the Night Before Last. Returned to Normal After Three Hours.

Epiphyllum has been regarded as an auspicious flower throughout the ages. Very few flower gardens in Shanghai grow it. This flower usually blooms once every few decades, and it always blooms at night. It is even less often seen. Things are valued for their rarity and occasional discovery.

Mistaken for Auspicious Sign

Zhongxi Girls' School at 11 Yidingpan Road in Shanghai was previously gifted several Epiphyllum plants by Guangdong native Huang Guiting. The school's landscape director, Miss Julia M. Wasson (Chinese name Wang Ziying), carefully cultivated them. It has been seven years now, and although they have been in bud all day, they have never been seen to bloom. Unexpectedly, the flower buds suddenly swelled and were about to bloom at dusk the day before yesterday (the 2nd). The landscape director realized that they were about to bloom, so she reported to the school principal, Yang Xizhen. The entire school was immediately stirred, and students separately notified friends by telephone. They gathered by the flowers and waited until 8:30 PM, when the petals gradually unfolded and opened. By 9:30 PM, they were in full bloom, with a total of thirty-five blooms. The yellow stamens and the original red stems and green leaves of the flowers created an infinitely delicate scene. After 10 PM, they gradually began to contract until 11:15 PM, when the flower buds closed and returned to their original state. When the flowers were in full bloom, the school specially invited artistic photographer Fu Yingguang to take several photos.

Public Works Department Library Book Category Ratios

Adding a Book Counter

The books in the Public Works Department Library are generally divided into two types: fiction and non-fiction. Fiction is the most popular among general readers, so the library purchases more fiction books. Recently, the library director drafted a list of books to be added and asked the Public Works Department Library Committee to review it. During the review, the committee mentioned the issue of the relative proportions of fiction and non-fiction books. In January 1932, the Library Committee stated that the proportion of non-fiction books exceeded the appropriate level and stipulated that when the library purchases new books, the ratio of fiction to non-fiction should generally be three to one. Therefore, the list of books to be added by the library this time also showed that the proportion of non-fiction books was too high. The Library Committee deleted eleven types of non-fiction books. In the future, the purchase of books will continue to be handled in accordance with the original ratio. In addition, the Public Works Department Library has cumbersome book borrowing procedures and is prone to errors in recording. In order to reduce the procedure and prevent the loss of books, it is planned to add a Dickman book counter, priced at more than 140 US dollars. The American manufacturer has agreed to ship the machine to Shanghai for a three-month trial. This machine was invented by the American Efficiency Promotion Bureau. Major libraries in Washington, New York, Philadelphia, and other cities have adopted it and achieved excellent results. In the future, when the Public Works Department Library is satisfied with the trial use, it will also purchase one, which will greatly benefit both the library and the readers.

Qiu Feihai Car Accident Case Verdict

Fine of 300 Yuan, Compensation of 2,000 Yuan

Qiu Feihai, a 35-year-old tennis player from Xiamen, residing at No. 5, Lane 217, Talas Road in the French Concession, was driving his private car No. 6474 on Foch Road from west to east at 6 AM on July 30th. Due to the driver's negligence, he hit Cui Zhen, the ten-year-old daughter of Huang Hanchen, a Jiangxi native residing at No. 29, Cihou Lane, Hartung Road, causing fatal injuries. Later, the father of the deceased, Huang Hanchen, hired lawyer Fan Gang to represent him in filing a private prosecution in the Second Special District Court, accusing Qiu Feihai of causing death due to negligence and requesting compensation for losses of 11,400 yuan in an accompanying civil lawsuit. The defendant, Qiu Feihai, also hired a lawyer to defend him. The debate concluded and a date was set for the verdict, as previously reported. Yesterday afternoon, when the time for the verdict arrived, both the plaintiff and defendant reported on time. Judge Xiong Huiping ascended the seat in the Second Court and ordered the two parties to be brought to the court to announce the verdict. The main text of the verdict was: Qiu Feihai is fined 300 yuan for causing death due to negligence. In the civil lawsuit, he shall compensate the plaintiff for losses of 2,000 yuan. If dissatisfied, they may appeal to the High Third Branch Court after receiving the verdict.

He Jieyuan's Daughter Disappears, Accuses Liao Yiwen of Enticement

Dismissed Due to Lack of Jurisdiction, Transferred to the District Court for Trial

Liao Yiwen, 24 years old, from Shouchang County, Zhejiang Province, has lived in Shanghai for many years. At first, he had no proper occupation, so his residence was uncertain. In September of the 21st year of the Republic (1932), Liao rented a room in the home of He Jieyuan, a Shaoxing native, at No. 29, Zonggongyi Car, Kulun Road, Zhabei, and became very close to He's children. He's daughter, who was only a teenager at the time and studying at a certain school, often secretly communicated with Liao behind her parents' backs. The following autumn, after Liao moved away, their correspondence became even more frequent. Liao also visited the school from time to time under various pretexts. He was unaware of this secret communication. Although He's younger brother had heard a little about it, he never told his sister-in-law about it. On the morning of August 24th of this year, He's daughter took advantage of her father's absence to write a letter to Liao at her desk. Unexpectedly, her mother saw it, and she was severely reprimanded. As a result, out of shame and anger, the daughter quietly left home and disappeared. On the same day, He's younger brother received a letter delivered by mail, signed by the daughter, but upon careful examination of the handwriting, it did not resemble her writing. The letter said that she could not bear the family's bullying and had fled to her ancestral home in Ningbo and Shaoxing. He immediately inquired in his hometown, but there was no trace of his daughter. Later, he learned about Liao's relationship with his daughter over the years and, based on the letters they had exchanged, concluded that his daughter's departure from home must have been due to Liao's enticement. However, He believed that since his daughter had already been betrothed to someone, it would be difficult to let her fly away. Therefore, he hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the First Special District Court against Liao for enticement, requesting that he be punished in accordance with Article 241, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law. The court had opened hearings twice, but the defendant could not be served, so the case could not be investigated. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Jiang continued the summons. The defendant and his defense lawyer surrendered to the court and stated that he was currently employed at the Dongfang Pharmacy at No. 620, Sichuan Road, and resided at a friend's place, but denied enticing the plaintiff's daughter. The court then asked He about the circumstances surrounding his daughter's disappearance. Because the incident occurred in the Chinese area, the court ruled that it lacked jurisdiction over the case and should transfer it to the Shanghai District Court for trial.

Elder Brother Accuses Younger Brother of Neglecting Support

Zhao Yousan Sues Zhao Peiwen, Must Investigate the Case Further Before Trial

Zhao Peiwen, a Tianjin native and owner of Zhenhua Cloth Store at No. 2, Shanxi Road (Pintang Lane), is the son of Zhao Lianyuan. Lianyuan is now 74 years old and lives in his hometown in Tianjin. He has five sons in total, and Peiwen is the fourth. He is now 41 years old. The eldest son, Zhao Yousan, is in his fifties and resides at No. 186, Ruihua Fang, Laozhenfu Road, French Concession. He and his younger brother Peiwen have never been on good terms. Recently, all the family's businesses have been controlled by Peiwen, causing the elder brother to live in poverty and have difficulty making a living. Therefore, he hired a lawyer to file a criminal private prosecution against Peiwen for abandonment. An elder brother accusing a younger brother of neglecting support has rarely occurred before. This type of lawsuit is probably a new development in the judicial organs of the Special District. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Huang of the First Special District Court opened the Fifth Court to summon both the plaintiff and defendant for questioning. According to the plaintiff, Zhao Yuer, the family property is worth about 60,000 to 70,000 yuan, all of which are controlled by the defendant. Zhenhua Cloth Store was founded in the 14th year of the Republic (1925) with a capital of 11,000 yuan, and is managed by the defendant. He used to give me 40 yuan per month, but suddenly stopped paying after March of the previous year. I have repeatedly negotiated with him, but he has refused, so I have filed a lawsuit. In response, the defendant, Zhao Peiwen, stated that his ancestors did not leave any property. Both Zhenhua and Huamao Cloth Stores were founded by me. The plaintiff has always been of bad character. He once wrote a letter of repentance. Because he never repented, I broke off relations with him, etc. The court held that the case still needed to be investigated, so it was decided to postpone the hearing and summon witnesses again for verification.

County Government Reissues Third-Term Opium Licenses

The Shanghai County's tobacco prohibition plan is based on the provincial government's regulations, which stipulate four years, shortened by one year, and is expected to be completely banned in three years. The county has already transferred young people to the county's opium rehabilitation center for treatment in order. The county government has found that the second-term opium addicts' licenses will expire at the end of September. However, the third-term licenses cannot be received and reissued as scheduled. Therefore, starting this month, the procedures for renewing the licenses will be carried out, that is, the words "Temporarily Replace Third-Term License" will be stamped on the second-term licenses.

Abduction and Prostitution of a Female Student Punished

Chen Xinyi, a 43-year-old man from Nanjing and a Catholic, had a daughter named Chen Zhiying, who was 19 years old this year. After graduating from a rural elementary school, she came to Shanghai two years ago and was admitted to the Xuhui Girls' Middle School, a Catholic school in Xujiahui, Shanghai, where she studied. On July 2nd of this year, the school began its summer vacation. The following morning at 9:00 AM, Zhiying accompanied a classmate home. They took a car to the North Station, where they met Cui Wang, a fellow Catholic and cousin of Zhiying's classmate, Jiao Yunying. (Cui Wang often visited the school to see Jiao, so she knew Zhiying.) Zhiying was forcibly taken to Cui's home at 32 Keller Road in the French Concession. First, Cui Wang's husband, Cui Kedong, seduced and defiled her. Then, under the pretext of recommending her for a nursing position, he made her write a voluntary statement and colluded with accomplices to force her into a brothel opened by a woman named Wang Zhang in Hengmao Lane No. 48, Baixianqiao, turning her into a prostitute. Zhiying languished in this hell for over a month before managing to send a letter to her parents. Her father, Chen Jiayi, came to Shanghai and reported the matter to the French police, who arrested Cui and his wife, as well as the madam Wang Zhang and a pimp named Xue Fengming. They were all handed over to the Second Special Court. The Police Department charged them under Articles 241 (Sections 1 and 2), 243, and 296 of the Criminal Law, for offenses against the family and offenses against freedom. After repeated interrogations and court debates, the trial concluded. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge Zhang Chaozuo presided over the First Criminal Court and sentenced Cui Kedong to eight years of imprisonment for abducting a woman under the age of twenty from her guardian for profit, and deprived him of his civil rights for eight years. Cui Wang and Wang Zhang were each sentenced to four years of imprisonment, and Xue Fengming was sentenced to one year of imprisonment.

Publication of Wu's English Calligraphy Practice Book

Mr. Wu Cishen, a teacher at Chengzhong Middle School on Tangshan Road in Hongkou, has been teaching English since graduating from St. John's University. For over a decade, he has achieved remarkable results. Recently, in order to enhance students' writing skills and improve the efficiency of English teaching, he compiled an English calligraphy practice book based on his decade of experience and wrote it in his own handwriting before investing in its printing and publication. In addition to the horizontal lines found in ordinary calligraphy practice books, this book also adds diagonal lines to indicate the slant of the letters. The letters in the book are printed in red, giving beginners the opportunity to trace over them in addition to copying them. The content is organized into eight volumes, starting with the uppercase letters of the alphabet and numbers, progressing from simple to complex, using the most frequently needed words in daily life, totaling as many as five to six thousand. Other content includes grammatical terms, sentence patterns, daily conversations, punctuation marks, maxims, famous world place names and personal names, letters, idioms, commercial terms, fables, scientific terms, and commonly used words in newspapers and magazines. Everything is included as much as possible. Practicing calligraphy with this book is like reading medicine. Its content is more than any other calligraphy practice book by at least one-fifth. With more opportunities for students to practice, their progress will naturally be faster. As for the quality of the printing, the beauty of the cover design, and the affordability of the price, these are secondary matters. The book was submitted to Director Pan of the Education Bureau and received a unique and insightful review. It has now been published successively and is sold at the Kaiming Bookstore on Simalu and at the author's publishing house.

Letter to the Editor

To the esteemed editor, I recently read in your newspaper about the Jardine Matheson comprador being threatened by bandits for extortion. However, the article stated that "it was found that Xi Bingxian, who used to be an accountant in the iron industry, resigned for some reason and has been borrowing money from the employer from time to time. Recently, last month, he went to ask for a loan but was refused and left in resentment. Perhaps this person is responsible for this incident." I was shocked to read this. Xi Bingxian has never worked as an accountant for our iron industry, nor did he ask me for a loan last month. He is an upright person and currently has a proper occupation at the Zhen Ting Sericulture School. He would never be involved in extortion. Fearing that this would damage Xi Bingxian's reputation, I dare to send this letter to inform you. I beg that your newspaper make a statement clarifying this matter tomorrow. Thank you very much. Sincerely, Dai Ziqing of Tianhe Foreign Firm, October 3rd.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits

— (Kangjianzhaifu)

Today is World Animal Day. The whole world, as usual, refrains from slaughtering for one day. At this time of extreme peril in the international situation, when the ambitious imperialists are preparing for the second great human slaughter of the twentieth century, those benevolent and righteous people are promoting kindness to animals. It is somewhat akin to the faint starlight visible in a remote corner of the sky amid the dark clouds.

"The benevolent love their relatives and then love the people, and love the people and then cherish things." This is the beginning of the great path of universal love. But in this era, there is no talk of loving the people, let alone cherishing things.

If humanity would only take a step back and reflect, using the Buddhist theory of cause and effect and reincarnation to console ourselves, perhaps humanity's self-slaughter is the karmic result of our past cruelty to other beings. From a materialistic historical perspective, the motive for humanity's self-slaughter still lies in the pursuit of survival. The desire to survive is the inherent nature of all things. How can we cherish the lives of other beings, delay the death penalty for all creatures by even one day, and reduce the millions upon millions of gallons of bloodshed? Perhaps this could alleviate even one ten-thousandth of humanity's own sins. This is more effective than the Kalachakra Tantra Dharma Assembly and the Pope's prayers for peace.

Absolute non-harm to animals, everyone knows, is an impossible thing. We take this Animal Day to propose a few universal principles for the protection of animals:

1. Animals that benefit humanity should not be harmed unless necessary.

2. Animals that have no benefit or harm to humanity should be allowed to coexist and thrive.

3. Animals that are harmful to humanity should be eliminated to reduce human suffering.

4. Before slaughtering animals, efforts should be made to shorten or reduce their suffering.

5. Animals kept as pets should have their suffering in captivity reduced as much as possible, restoring their freedom and naturalness.

Animal Day

— Qiulang

"Even ants and insects cherish their lives!" We can know that all living things in the world love life and hate death. However, cruel humans, using their agile minds, exploit them to serve humanity, and even slaughter parts of them (such as cattle, sheep, pigs, chickens, ducks, etc.) to be used as food or delicacies for people to feast on! However, we must also distinguish between animals that can be used to serve humans or are beneficial to humanity. It is absolutely inappropriate to use them as food and they must be carefully protected. If they are animals that are not beneficial to humans, it is not impossible to use them as meat on the table. Furthermore, beasts such as jackals, wolves, tigers, and leopards are not only useless to people, but also endanger human life, so they must be eliminated.

Today is World Animal Day. The Shanghai China Animal Protection Association will hold its second propaganda conference this afternoon at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and will also hold a general membership meeting. Major newspapers will publish special Animal Day supplements, and movie theaters will add promotional films. Furthermore, it has been requested that the Executive Yuan's Ministry of the Interior issue a circular to all provinces, cities, and counties in the country, requiring them to stop slaughtering animals for one day on this day. All of these measures can be said to have exhausted the meaning of protecting animals. However, animals are, after all, animals. The flood victims in the disaster areas, who are one level above animals, are crying out for food. It is hoped that the gentlemen of the Animal Protection Association will transfer their benevolence in caring for animals to find ways to relieve the disaster victims, which would be an immeasurable virtue!

Continuing "Shanghai's Pull"

— Zuichi Sheng

Reading the previous article "Shanghai's Pull" in this journal, I felt that there were several kinds of "pulling" facts that had not yet been mentioned. Now, I might as well talk about them to join in the fun.

In the evening, if you walk through a certain section of Avenue Edward VII, you will see small hotels lined up on that side. Some, resembling tea houses, stand or sit at the door. Even if you don't look at them, they will enthusiastically greet you. "Hey, sir, do you want a room? Or a girl, a real virgin, guaranteed to be good. Do you want to open a room and have some fun?" Even if you shake your head to indicate no, they will keep nagging you. This kind of "pull" has two meanings. It is somewhat different from a prostitute soliciting customers.

A few years ago, I was strolling on the road at night. Someone would softly say to you: "Do you want to go to the club? Inside there is pai gow, there is shaking stalls, there is.... Guaranteed you won't get into trouble." However, in recent years, the foreign concessions have been very strict with gambling prohibitions. This kind of "pull" is no longer common.

One day, I was walking through Nanshi. There were quite a few opium dens open there. Seeing these mysterious shops, I couldn't help but pay attention to them. Suddenly, someone wearing short clothes ran over and said, "Sir, do you want to smoke opium? We have aged paste, new beds, and women to prepare the pipe for you." This happened twice in a row. Unfortunately, I am not a leisurely person and don't have the qualifications to inhale smoke. Otherwise, hearing these tempting words, I would really salivate three feet!

In the area around Dongmen Road, Shiliupu, Nanshi, if you take a rickshaw with bedding and luggage, someone will follow you or grab the rickshaw pole and greet you: "Are you going on the ×× Lun ship? Do you want ship tickets?" This kind of "pull" can also be seen often.

Furthermore, when the Lun ships at various places dock at the wharf, the passengers disembark one after another: many rickshaw pullers will swarm forward to solicit business. If you have luggage, it will be very troublesome. Letting them snatch and grab from each other will either result in material losses or they will try to rip you off. There are also dock thugs who take the opportunity to rob people. This kind of "pull" is very harmful to travelers and should be strictly prohibited!

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 19: The Chief Clerk Cherishes His Reputation, Knowing How to Knock on Doors; New Love Leaves Flesh and Blood, No Way to Visit the Sick

Shi Lian waved his hand and said, "You don't need to say it, I know everything. Now I'm asking you, what kind of illness are you suffering from? Why are you sitting at the gate?" The old woman shook her head and said, "I don't know what kind of illness it is either. But I feel very flustered. I can't lie in bed, I want to sit here and look at my granddaughter." Shi Lian smiled and said, "Isn't that a joke? Her place is several courtyards away from this back door, how can you see her?" In the old woman's lackluster eyes, tears actually flowed. She said in a trembling voice, "Yes, I can't see her, but I feel better sitting here." As she spoke, she dragged the sleeve of her right hand with her left hand, and kept rubbing her eyes. Shi Lian felt sad when he saw her like this. He stood there blankly for a while, and then looked at the gate of her house. He asked, "This is very strange. You are a sick old woman sitting outside the gate, why don't your family members come out to see you?" The old woman said, "My daughter-in-law is also sitting here, accompanying me. I'm hoping for my granddaughter, doesn't she hope for her daughter?" She went to boil water for me to drink. My relative, Sister Hu, is probably angry and doesn't comfort us anymore." As she said this, she seemed to be struggling to speak, so she leaned her head against the wall and closed her eyes slightly. Shi Lian said, "Old woman, how long have you been waiting here?" She opened her eyes and raised her two crooked fingers upwards. Shi Lian said, "Oh! You've been sitting here for two days." The old woman nodded twice. Shi Lian said, "Old woman, your granddaughter is fine, she wanted to come to see you, but..." The old woman quickly interrupted, "What? Did Master Jia let her out?" As she said this, she supported the wall and suddenly stood up. However, she was ultimately standing up too quickly. With this sudden rush upwards, she was excited, but then she fell downwards, almost falling to the ground. How could an old woman who was not far from death withstand such a fall? When Shi Ying saw this, he felt sweat pouring down his body. (332)

Records of the Imperial Incense

— Original work by Princess Der Ling of Qing, translated by Qin Shouou

(Unnumbered Chapter) Meeting of the Author and Translator

One morning, the newspapers all published the news of her departure from Shanghai to the north. I knew that if I wanted to see her, I couldn't delay any longer. However, I also knew that my temper was too bad, and I couldn't stand the sight of those foreign servants in洋行 (foreign companies) and the so-called "俊歐 (handsome Europeans)." Therefore, I deliberately waited until about 3:20 in the afternoon before going to the North Railway Station with a belly full of curiosity, to pay a very hurried and impolite visit.

Walking into the platform and along the row of blue carriages that stood out like a crane among chickens, I found a chubby, middle-aged woman's face in the first window. Her makeup was very heavy, and a black Western hat was pressed low on her forehead. Below were two very fluent but not very large black eyes and a flat nose. With just this one glance, I knew that the person I wanted to see was in front of me.

It was a first-class sleeper compartment on the Shanghai-Ping train. The furnishings were, of course, extremely luxurious. Our old princess was wearing a fashionable blue Western suit, and a string of bright cherry-like red glass beads hung around her neck (or perhaps they were treasures, who knows?). She was sitting inside, very appropriately. I knocked a few times on the open door – even I couldn't avoid acting Western, given her Western air. As usual, she said "Come in" and stood up to greet me at the doorway.

I am a tall person, and she only reached my chest when she stood up, so I still felt she was a bit too fat and too short, not as tall as a "real foreigner," but compared to the women of our country, she could probably be ranked in the first class.

She must have been influenced by the Old Buddha (Empress Dowager Cixi). Although she had lost her youth, she still loved to dress up. The scent of perfume kept wafting into my nostrils. When I shook her hand, I saw that her fingernails were also dyed with very red nail polish. To be honest, she really looked very young, only like someone in their mid-thirties, and couldn't be called an old lady!

After exchanging names and briefly introducing myself, I asked her if she could spare some time when she returned to Shanghai from Beijing to discuss a few questionable points about "Records of the Imperial Incense." She immediately declared very sincerely that the book was written too hastily, and errors were inevitable, so she very much approved of my being able to discuss it with her in detail when she returned south. She also hoped to have the entire translation that I had done sent to her to look at. This made me a little apprehensive. To be honest, my translation was really not something to be shown in public, but since she had this hope, I would have to bite the bullet and send it to her anyway. (Two)

People Waiting for War

Biographies

Painter Gao Jianfu

— Zhen Lü

In the Chinese Western painting world, the leading figures in recent years have been the two gentlemen, Liu and Xu. However, at present, Mr. Gao Jianfu, who had long stood out but has been concealing himself, has risen to form a three-legged balance of power.

If we observe from the art itself, Gao has his own unique value, worthy of admiration. His paintings, which combine Chinese and Western methods, first had the foundation of the spiritual portrayal of traditional Chinese painting, and then added the realism of Western painting, discarding the dross of both sides and preserving their essence, and integrating them with his genius, so he can stand out as a unique and aesthetic school. One of his paintings, for people who have both Chinese and Western painting literacy to appreciate, will never make one side feel uncomfortable.

I originally had no personal connection with Gao, but I remember that my one-sided spiritual acquaintance with him began as early as the third or fourth year of the Republic of China. At that time, he was starting a store specializing in beauty and health products, located diagonally opposite the Commercial Press on Qipan Street, called the "Aesthetic Bookstore." The store sold printed framed pictures, art postcards, painting collections, and plaster statues, etc. Sometimes there were also Gao's and other famous artists' genuine works exhibited for sale. At that time, I was only twelve or thirteen years old. I didn't study painting myself, but I loved to read books, especially Gao's paintings, for which I had a special fondness. I occasionally saw the scrolls, etc., made by him in the old Chinese method of mounting, and I admired his unique, rich aura and harmonious colors. I would always linger and look at them for a while, with a reluctance to leave and a sense of satisfaction! Therefore, I gradually became associated with the Aesthetic Bookstore—probably a natural psychological manifestation of "love me, love my dog (愛屋及烏) —even to the point of —love my dog's house (愛烏及屋)." But unfortunately, I was young and had no money to buy paintings. I had no choice but to seek the next best thing, and every time I passed the Aesthetic Bookstore, I would often buy several kinds of art postcards, mostly collotype reduced prints of Gao's paintings. After that, a large portion of the pocket money I got in childhood was spent on this. After three or four years, my interest gradually faded due to diversification, and after some time, I passed Qipan Street again, and I didn't see the Aesthetic Bookstore. I don't know when the store moved or closed down.

A few years ago, the West Lake Exposition was held. I rushed to visit the exposition near its closing, and I had my first meeting with West Lake. I unexpectedly saw this long-lost painting by Gao in the art gallery, which was full of countless fine works by ancient and modern people. Although there were only two or five works, it was enough to create the pleasant association of "old friends and new acquaintances meeting at the same time!"

Now, this painter Gao has been fortunate enough to be recognized in his lifetime and has received a well-deserved reputation. I also feel sympathetic satisfaction! The situation is not entirely appropriate: poverty, prosperity, obscurity, and fame all change with the times, and praise, criticism, suppression, and promotion are inevitably flawed. Gao's current environment can be considered a blessing of luck. How many people in the world are truly given their due and receive fair recognition? However, I disagree with someone adding the honorable title of "revolutionary painter" to Gao, whether because he himself had worked hard for the National Revolution, or because his works contain revolutionary qualities. In terms of his career, revolution is revolution, and painter is painter, which are originally two different jobs and cannot be confused. In terms of his works, labeling them as revolutionary is not enough to summarize and fully express his strengths. This kind of undeserved praise is probably not helpful to the recipient, and for the speaker, it is loving in the wrong way!

Letter to the Editor: Respected Editor, I have been suffering from lung disease for a long time. Treatment in Beijing was ineffective. In early spring, I wrote to you asking you to publish a notice seeking effective remedies, and also to inquire about the effectiveness of Yijincao (益金草). I was grateful that you responded in the Chunqiu column, saying that soliciting prescriptions had many drawbacks, but that Mrs. Huang, a colleague of yours, had taken Yijincao and found it very effective, and advised me to try it. I immediately followed your advice and purchased it from Peisheng Pharmaceutical Company in Rendeli, Zhaozhou Road, Shanghai. In less than a month, the disease was cured. It has been more than half a year since then, and there has been no recurrence, so I am certain that it has been completely cured. With gratitude, I am writing to thank you and request that you publish the original letter in Chunqiu so that those suffering from the same disease can find a beacon. I hope you will not refuse. Sincerely, Liang Boxin

Sports News

Sixth National Games: Opening Ceremony Parade Arrangements

The ranks must be strict, and the clothing should strive for uniformity. When passing the West Rostrum, march in goose step and give the eye salute. The order of the national martial arts and the number of participants in each unit were announced yesterday.

The National Games has formulated the following measures for the parade of officials and athletes at the opening ceremony:

(1) Officials, referees, and athletes of each participating unit should assemble at 9:15 a.m. on the 10th on the cinder track behind the East Rostrum, and be lined up by 9:45 a.m., ready for departure.

(2) The assembly point for each unit is marked by the unit flag prepared by the organizing committee. Officials and athletes are arranged in four ranks in the following order:

(1) Unit flag, held by one person and supported by two people; (2) Chief leader; (3) Female instructors and managers; (4) Male instructors and managers; (5) Female athletes; (6) Male athletes.

(3) The clothing of the athletes in each unit should strive for uniformity.

(4) During the parade, the national flag, party flag, games flag, and military band will lead the way, followed by the officials and referees of the organizing committee, and then the officials and athletes of the other units in the following order (also arranged in order during assembly): (1) Shaanxi, (2) Shandong, (3) Tibet, (4) Philippines, (5) Qingdao, (6) Shanxi, (7) Jiangxi, (8) Hebei, (9) Zhejiang, (10) Henan, (11) Hubei, (12) Weihaiwei, (13) Harbin, (14) Heilongjiang, (15) Liaoning, (16) Nanjing, (17) Guangxi, (18) Fujian, (19) Jiangsu, (20) Peiping, (21) Anhui, (22) Xikang, (23) Xinjiang, (24) Mongolia, (25) Qinghai, (26) Suiyuan, (27) Hong Kong, (28) Guangdong, (29) Malaya, (30) Sichuan, (31) Hunan, (32) Guizhou, (33) Java, (34) Jilin, (35) Rehe, (36) Yunnan, (37) Chahar, (38) Shanghai.

(5) During the parade, each unit should be eight steps apart from the unit in front and behind, and officials and athletes should be four steps apart from each other. Each small row should be steps apart from the row in front and behind, do not stray too far or be too close.

(6) The parade route is to enter through the main gate of the East Rostrum, turn right and walk along the runway, pass in front of the West Rostrum, and turn into the center of the field at the southeast corner, facing the Rostrum. The remaining units will turn towards the Rostrum one by one, and stand at a distance of five meters from the runway.

(7) When passing the West Rostrum during the parade, march in goose step and give the eye salute to the right to show respect.

(8) After passing the West Rostrum, the officials and referees of the organizing committee will take turns ascending the official and referee stands on the Rostrum and do not have to continue to advance.

(9) After the ceremony, return to the outside of the East Rostrum in the original order and disperse.

Number of National Martial Arts Participants

Special Train Service on the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations, as the Sixth National Games will be held in the Shanghai Central District Sports Center, with the games scheduled for eleven days, from October 10th to 20th, have decided to operate special passenger trains to facilitate the round trips of spectators from all stations on the two lines. On the Beijing-Shanghai Line, a special passenger train will be operated from Beijing to Shanghai on October 9th, and a special passenger train will be operated from Shanghai to Beijing on October 21st. Tickets will only be sold to and from the stations of Shangbei (上北, likely referring to a station near Shanghai North), Suzhou, Wuxi, Changzhou, Zhenjiang, and Nanjing. On the Shanghai-Hangzhou Line, a special passenger train will be operated from Zhabei to Shanghai on October 9th, and a special passenger train will be operated from Shanghai to Zhabei on October 21st. Tickets will only be sold to and from the stations of Shangbei (上北), Songjiang, Jiashan, Jiaxing, Xiashi, Changan, Hangzhou, and Zhakou. Each of these trains will have approximately nine first, second, and third class carriages. Passengers who are not traveling to Shanghai to visit the National Games may also ride. However, the number of tickets sold will be limited to the number of seats on the train. Special round-trip tickets to Shangbei (上北) will be sold at the designated ticket stations, with first and second class tickets discounted by 25% from the ordinary fare, and third class tickets discounted by 15% from the ordinary fare. The validity period will be fourteen days and tickets may be sold from October 8th. Single tickets of each class should be charged according to the express train fare, and round-trip tickets of each class to stations other than Shangbei (上北) should also be charged according to the express train regulations and fees, with the validity period limited to seven days.

Traffic Control Measures

During the Games, there will definitely be a large number of visitors. In order to avoid traffic congestion, the Public Works Bureau has widened the roads such as Xiangyin Road, and the Public Utilities Bureau has designated the following four roads as one-way streets: West Sports Association Road, Qimei Road, Huangxing Road, and East Sports Association Road. The routes for all types of vehicles, such as private cars, commercial passenger cars, public buses, and freight trucks, have also been decided by the Public Utilities Bureau in consultation with the relevant bureaus. The parking locations for private cars have been designated in the north of the stadium, with a total of seventeen locations, each with a parking sign and number. When each car arrives at the stadium, a piece of paper will be issued by the organizing committee, with the designated parking space printed on it. Each private car should park in the designated space in order. All traffic routes and parking locations have been drawn into a map. Citizens who wish to obtain this map can go to the Vehicle Management Office of the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, or the China Travel Service at 420 Sichuan Road, or the News Inspection Office at 306 Continental Department Store, etc., to obtain it.

Additional Public Buses

During the Games, in order to facilitate spectators, the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, the Public Bus Management Office, the Zhabei Chinese Public Bus Company, the Shanghai-Minhang and Shanghai-Bao and Xihu Long-Distance Bus Companies have mobilized many vehicles to run special buses to facilitate transportation. The starting and ending points and fares of these public buses are listed below:

According to the starting points of the above routes, Huangxing Road is the furthest from the center of the concession. Spectators who want to avoid congestion can board the bus there. Although the converted freight vehicles on Zhengda Road are simpler, there are many vehicles there that depart at any time, which may reduce congestion.

In addition, the Municipal Public Utilities Bureau believes that there should be connections between the Chinese and Concession boundaries to facilitate passengers. It has ordered the Chinese Public Bus Company to contact the British Public Bus Company to extend the first route of the Chinese company to the back gate of Hongkou Park on Jiangwan Road (i.e., Tongli Road) as the terminal, in order to connect with the public buses in the Special Zone.

Sichuan Football Team　Yesterday Lost to Guanghua

Guanghua Has Xu Luo and Other Generals Serving, Greatly Increasing Their Reputation　The Sichuan Team Lacked Coordination, Resulting in a Miserable Defeat of Two to Six　—Today the Sichuan Team Plays the South China Team—

The Sichuan Province All-China Games football team had a practice match with the Guanghua football team at 3:30 PM yesterday at the Guanghua field. The Sichuan team arrived at the school at 3:00 PM. The Guanghua Sichuan Alumni Association specially posted slogans, warmly welcoming them. The team was organized by the 4th Division football team of the 21st Army of Sichuan. The players' uniforms consisted of blue wool coats and gray wool trousers, with a team emblem on the left lapel, which was quite dignified and beautiful. Yesterday, in their first test, they lost to Guanghua by two to six. However, the spirit of the team's players was admirable. Unfortunately, they had courage but lacked strategy. The coordination of the forwards was poor, and they missed many opportunities. If they could pay attention to this, they would be quite promising. I hope all the athletes will strive to compete for a place in the All-China Games. The details of yesterday's match are recorded as follows:

First Half　Guanghua Feels the Momentum

At 3:30 PM, referee Jiang Jingnan blew his whistle, and both sides deployed their formations and started the battle. Guanghua's forward Xu Jingcheng is a brave general from Donghua, and Luo Douwen and Jiang Zhaoxiang are also leaders among the youth team. The three forwards coordinated well. In less than ten minutes, Xu Jingcheng got the ball in the center and passed it to Douwen. Little Luo flew up with a kick, and the ball went right into the corner of the net, opening the scoring. The Sichuan team tried hard to counterattack. Zeng Zhengqi led the crowd, opening the way forward. Guanghua's defense was weak, and they were penetrated deep into their territory. Unfortunately, Zeng Zhengqi's shot was inaccurate and did not hit the target. After a period of melee, Xu Jingcheng showed his great power. Luo and Jiang worked hard to respond. The ball often hovered in front of the Sichuan team's goal. Within twenty minutes, Little Xu scored four consecutive goals. Guanghua took the lead with five to zero. Although the Sichuan team tried hard to recover the lost ground, the coordination of the forwards was not good enough, and they missed many good opportunities. The first half ended with this.

Second Half　Sichuan Team Slightly Wins

Changing sides and fighting again, due to the disparity in strength between the two sides, Guanghua's Luo Douwen retired, and Xu Jingcheng was transferred to defense, which slightly evened the odds. The Sichuan team players still worked hard to fight, not discouraged by the defeat. Their spirit was commendable. The five forwards ran quite fast, but the passing was too slow, so they could not get what they wanted. After a period of melee, Zhong Shijin shot a high ball from the center line. The landing point was ten yards from the goal. Guanghua's defender Zhao Aisheng hooked it with his left foot, and the ball went straight into his own goal. Ling Xuan could not react in time and lost a goal. Not long after, Zeng Zhengqi attacked again, breaking through three barriers, and lightly passed to Ma Zuyin, who swept his foot, and the ball went into the net. After the Sichuan team scored two consecutive goals, their momentum was stronger. Guanghua's Jiang Zhaoxiang took advantage of the enemy's rear defense being lax, and stole a camp, secretly crossing the Chencang, and recovered a goal. Soon the time was up. Calculating the total, Guanghua won a big victory over the Sichuan team with six to one. The lineups were as follows:

Guanghua Team

Chen Zhijie (up), Ling Xuan (down), Zhao Aisheng, Zheng Dequan (up), Xu Jingcheng (down), Yao Zhenggang, Shi Cheng, Zhou Yanyi (up), Dai Gongbei (down), Chen Shigeng, Luo Douwen (up), Deng Ruiai (down), Xu Jingcheng (up), Li Zumian (down), Jiang Zhaoxiang, Dong Changzhao (up), Gu Dingxiang (down)

Sichuan Team

Li Pingxi, Ye Ziming, Lü Shu, Wang Yongkun (down), You Dezhao, Liu Guoquan (up), He Rongzhong, Huang Weixiao (down), Ma Zuyin, Zeng Zhengqi, Zhou Tailin, Zhong Shijin (up), Yun Chongqing

Also, in order to get more practice opportunities, the Sichuan football team has scheduled another match with the local South China football team at Fudan University at 3:30 PM this afternoon.

Football Friendly Match　Donghua Wins Hujiang Six to Two

The Donghua football team accepted an invitation from Hujiang University yesterday to play a friendly match at the university's field in Yangshupu. Overall, the match yesterday was one-sided from beginning to end, so there was not much excitement. The audience was only a few dozen students from the university. As a result, four to one, Donghua won a big victory.

At the beginning of the second half, Donghua kicked off first. In a few minutes, Yang Xiqi of Hujiang opened the scoring first. Seeing the enemy in full swing, Donghua was brave and energetic. Li Yichen immediately returned one goal. Ten minutes later, Li Youpei scored two goals. From then on, the army's prestige was greatly enhanced and invincible. The crowd also received a long pass from Chen Jiaqiu and scored a beautiful goal with a ground shot. The first half ended with four to one. After changing sides, there was a long period of melee. Li Yichen of Donghua received a pass from Tang Qiuting and headed the ball into the net. Soon after, he scored another goal. Quan of Hujiang scored, but Wu Jingqiu pulled back a goal. By then, the overall situation was set. Li Yangchen contributed a lot to Donghua's victory. In total, six to one, Hujiang was defeated.

Famous Sports Book　Diagrams of Track and Field Training Published

Written by Lawson, an American Track and Field Instructor Who Attended the World Games

Lawson and Sacki, American track and field instructors who attended the World Games, based on their experience in guiding track and field competitions, compiled a book called Diagrams of Track and Field Training. The original book is priced at eight yuan, so its value can be imagined. The Fen Publishing House at 392 Laoshifu Road, Shanghai, specially invited Mr. Jiang Lianggui, a teacher at the East Asia Sports Academy, to translate the book into Chinese, and Mr. Wu Yun meticulously proofread it. The book has now been published. Its content is divided into twelve chapters, including: 1. Javelin, 2. High Jump, 3. Discus, 4. Shot Put, 5. Pole Vault, 6. Short Distance Running, 7. Middle Distance Running, 8. Long Distance Running, 9. High Hurdles, 10. Low Hurdles, 11. Relay Race. Each item has dozens of illustrations. The whole book is mainly illustrations, with more than a hundred pictures in total, supplemented by simple text explanations, which makes it extremely easy for beginners to imitate. The price per copy is eight dimes, and an additional 11 cents for registered postage outside Shanghai. The sales department of the Qinfen Publishing House at 177 Simalu Road, Shanghai, also sells it.

Education News

Ministry of Education　Notice to Hold Screening Examination

The Ministry of Education announced that it will hold a screening examination on November 10 this year in Beiti, Shanghai, for graduates and students of unregistered and closed private colleges and universities. All graduates and students of unregistered and closed private colleges and universities who, when they entered school, had one of the following qualifications: (1) graduated from a senior high school or equivalent school; (2) graduated from an old-style middle school or completed two years of preparatory courses for university after completing one year of senior high school; (3) graduated from an old-style middle school or equivalent school and served for two years; must apply to the Beiping Municipal Social Bureau or the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau before October 31. In addition, all students of colleges and universities who are graduates of unregistered and closed private high schools or equivalent schools may also take the screening examination. However, the subjects of the examination are limited to basic subjects. This is a special notice.
